Al-Shirazi's Use of Qalb Against the Ash'ari Argument
Al-Shirazi's qalb refutation of the Ash'ari argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze al-Shirazi's qalb refutation of the Ash'ari argument on the command form.

Core Idea
Al-Shirazi inverts the Ash'ari argument to show it proves the opposite of their claim.

This lesson examines a historical example of qalb from Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. He refutes the Ash'ari claim that the imperative form (amr) has no linguistic meaning indicating action by turning their own reasoning against them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Ash'ari argument
Identify the Ash'ari claim: the command form has no set linguistic meaning. Their proof: establishing such a meaning requires reason or transmission; reason cannot, and transmission must be mutawatir or ahad; both fail. Outline this structure.
2
Identify the 'illa used
The 'illa (cause) is the impossibility of establishing the meaning due to the constraints on transmission. Note that the Ash'aris assume their own position (ambiguity) is established.
3
See al-Shirazi's inversion
Al-Shirazi applies the exact same ‘illa to the Ash'ari claim that the command form is ambiguous (ishtirak). He shows that the same reasoning leads to the conclusion that ambiguity cannot be established either.
4
Confirm the refutation
Conclude that the Ash'ari argument is self-defeating. By qalb, their own proof is turned against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القلب : هو في اصطلاح الأصول عبارة عن ربط خلاف ما قاله المستدل بعلته للإلحاق بأصله. وفي اللغة على معنيين : أحدهما جعل أعلى الشيء أسفل، ومنه أخذ قلب العلة حكمًا وبالعكس، لأن العلة أعلى من الحكم لكونها أصلا، والحكم أسفل لكونه تبعا . . والثاني : جعل ظاهر الشيء باطنا كقلب الجراب ومنه أخذ قلب الوصف شاهدا على الخصم بعد أن يكون شاهدا للخصم والمقصود بالقلب في اصطلاحنا هو الاستدلال على الخصم بمثل ما استدل به ويسميه الجويني بالاشتراك، ويعرفه بأنه : مساواة الخصم خصمه فيما يورده على التنافي مثال ذلك عند الأصوليين، ما نجده عند أبي إسحاق الشيرازي رحمه الله حيث أورد استدلال الأشاعرة، ومنهم القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني على أن الأمر لا صيغة له تدل على الفعل، بقولهم : إثبات صيغة الأمر إنما يكون بالعقل أو النقل ؛ فلا يجوز أن يكون بالعقل، لأن العقل لا مجال له في إثبات الأسامي واللغات لأنها لو كانت معلومة بالعقل لما احتيج إلى قراءة كتب الأدب والمصنفات في اللغة وسماعها من أهل الخبرة بها، وإن كان طريق إثباتها بالنقل فلا يخلو إما أن يكون النقل تواترا أو آحادًا، فإن كان تواترا وجب أن يقع العلم به ضرورة لكل أحد، لأن ما طريقه الضرورات يشترك العقلاء في معرفته، ولو كان كذلك لعلمناه كما علمتم، فثبت أنه لا تواتر فيه، وإن كان آحادًا فلا يثبت به لأنه أصل من الأصول، وإثبات أصل من الأصول بأخبار الآحاد لا يجوز، فلا وجه لإثبات ذلك». ولأن الشيرازي يقول بأن للأمر صيغة موضوعة في اللغة تدل على الفعل، فإنه لم يرتض هذا الاستدلال واعترض عليه بطريق القلب، حيث استخدم هذا الدليل في الاحتجاج على الخصم، وبين أن هذا الدليل هو حجة على الخصم وليس حجة له ، فقال : والجواب : أنا نقلب ذلك عليه في إثبات الاشتراك في هذه الصيغة، فإنه يزعم أنها تحتمل الإقدام وتحتمل الإحجام وهي مشتركة بين الأمرين، فلا يخلو إما أن يكون قد أثبت هذا الاشتراك بالعقل أو بالنقل، فلا يجوز أن يكون بالعقل، لأن العقل لا مجال له في ذلك على ما ذكروا، ولا يجوز أن يكون بالنقل، لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون تواترا لأنه لو وجد لعلمناه ضرورة كما علمنا سائر الأضداد والألفاظ المشتركة كالعين واللون، ولا يجوز أن يكون آحادًا لأن مثل ذلك لا يثبت بأخبار الآحاد ، لأنه يكثر استعماله وتعم البلوى به فلا يكون النقل فيه آحادًا، فكل عذر له في إثبات الاشتراك فهو عذرنا في إثبات كونه صيغة موضوعة لاستدعاء (الفعل)
Al-qalb: In the terminology of usul, it is an expression for linking the opposite of what the mutadallil (arguer) said with its 'illa (cause) for attaching to its origin. Linguistically, it has two meanings: first, making the upper part of something lower, from which is taken the inversion of the cause in ruling and vice versa, because the cause is higher than the ruling as it is a root, and the ruling is lower as it is a branch. Second, making the outer part of something inner, like turning a bag inside out, from which is taken the inversion of the description as a witness against the opponent after it was a witness for the opponent. What is intended by al-qalb in our terminology is to argue against the opponent by means similar to what he argued with, and al-Juwayni calls it al-ishtirak (sharing), and defines it as: the opponent equaling his opponent in what he presents in opposition. An example of that with the usuliyyin is what we find with Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, may Allah have mercy on him, where he presented the argument of the Ash'aris, including al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, that the command (al-amr) has no linguistic form indicating the action, by their statement: 'The establishment of the form of command can only be by reason or transmission; it cannot be by reason, because reason has no scope in establishing names and languages, for if they were known by reason, there would be no need to read books of literature and works on language and hear them from experts. If the way of establishing them is by transmission, then it cannot be other than either mutawatir (massively transmitted) or ahad (single reports). If it is mutawatir, knowledge of it would necessarily occur to everyone, because what is known by necessities is shared by rational people in knowing it, and if it were so, we would know it as you know; so it is established that there is no tawatur in it. If it is ahad, then it cannot be established because it is a fundamental principle, and establishing a fundamental principle by ahad reports is not permissible, so there is no way to establish that.' And because al-Shirazi says that the command has a linguistic form indicating the action, he did not accept this argument and objected by way of qalb, using this argument in disputation against the opponent, and showed that this argument is a proof against the opponent and not for him. He said: The answer: I invert that against him in establishing ishtirak (ambiguity) in this form, for he claims that it can imply action and can imply omission and is shared between the two matters. Then it cannot be other than that he has established this ishtirak either by reason or transmission. It cannot be by reason, because reason has no scope in that according to what they mentioned. And it cannot be by transmission, because it cannot be other than either mutawatir, for if it existed we would know it necessarily as we know other opposites and ambiguous words like 'ayn and lawn, and it cannot be ahad because such a thing is not established by ahad reports, because it is widely used and the need for it is general, so transmission about it cannot be ahad. So every excuse he has in establishing ishtirak is our excuse in establishing that it is a form set for demanding action.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage defines qalb (inversion/reversal), a key dialectical technique in jadal, and illustrates it with a detailed example from Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. The author begins by giving the technical definition of qalb in usul al-fiqh: linking the opposite of what the arguer said with its cause (illa) to attach it to its origin (asl). This means the opponent takes the same reasoning used by the arguer and applies it to the opponent's own position. The author then notes two linguistic meanings of qalb: (1) turning something upside down, and (2) turning something inside out. Both are relevant to the technical usage, where the cause (illa) and ruling are 'inverted'. The specific jadal definition is then given: arguing against the opponent by means similar to what he argued with. Al-Juwayni calls this 'ishtirak' (sharing), meaning the opponent equals the arguer in what he presents as opposition. The example is from al-Shirazi's refutation of the Ash'ari claim that the imperative form (amr) has no linguistic meaning indicating action. The Ash'aris argued that the meaning of the command form can only be established by reason or transmission. Reason cannot do it. Transmission must be either mutawatir (massively transmitted) or ahad (single reports). It cannot be mutawatir because everyone would know it, and it cannot be ahad because it is a fundamental principle. Al-Shirazi inverts this argument: he applies the same reasoning to the Ash'ari claim that the command form is ambiguous (ishtirak between action and omission). He shows that the Ash'aris themselves cannot establish this ambiguity by reason or transmission either. If they claim it is established by mutawatir transmission, then everyone would know it, but they don't. If by ahad, then it fails because it is a widely used matter. Thus, their argument is turned against them. This illustrates the essence of qalb: using the opponent's own proof structure to refute his position.

The Structure of Ilzam in Jadal: Definition and Example
Author defines ilzam and gives al-Juwayni's objection to the Mu'tazila on hazr before revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of ilzam and trace al-Juwayni's dialectical move against the Mu'tazilite prohibitionists.

Core Idea
Ilzam forces the opponent to accept a consequence that contradicts his own position.

In this passage, the author defines ilzam and gives an example from al-Juwayni against the Mu'tazila. Ilzam is a powerful dialectical tool: you compel the opponent to recognize a necessary logical consequence of his own view that undermines it. Al-Juwayni uses ilzam to show that the Mu'tazilite position on prohibition before revelation leads to an absurdity. By carefully parsing this example, you will learn how ilzam works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of ilzam
Find the sentence where al-Juwayni defines ilzam. Notice the key phrase: 'دفع كلام الخصم بما يوجب فصلا بينه وبين ما تضمن نصرته'. What does 'fasl' (separation) mean in this context?
Ilzam is about forcing a separation between the opponent and his own advocated position.
2
Identify the two Mu'tazilite positions on pre-revelation actions
The passage states that the Mu'tazila split into two groups: one held that actions before revelation are prohibited (hazr), the other that they are permissible (ibaha). Note these two views.
This sets up the target of al-Juwayni's ilzam: the prohibitionists.
3
Analyze al-Juwayni's objection to the prohibitionists
Al-Juwayni presents three possibilities for how the prohibitionists could specify what is prohibited. First, prohibit all actions. Second, prohibit some without rational basis. Third, prohibit only those that one can avoid. For each, he shows a flaw.
This is the core of the ilzam: each option leads to a problem.
4
Understand why each option fails
If they prohibit all actions, it's an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yusta'). If they prohibit arbitrarily, the view collapses. If they prohibit only avoidable actions, that still begs the question of how to determine avoidability.
The ilzam is effective because the opponent cannot escape the dilemma.
5
Formulate the ilzam as a dialectical dilemma
Summarize the argument: The prohibitionists must either prohibit everything (impossible) or specify some actions (arbitrary or circular). Therefore, their position is untenable. This is the 'necessitation' that separates them from their advocacy.
This logical structure is the essence of ilzam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و - الإلزام : عرفه الجويني بأنه : دفع كلام الخصم بما يوجب فصلا بينه وبين ما تضمن نصرته. من ذلك ما اعترض به الجويني على كل من فرق المعتزلة ، قال : وقد افترقت المعتزلة، فذهب بعضهم إلى أن ما لا يعين العقل فيه قبحًا ولا حسنًا فهو على الحظر قبل ورود الشرع، وذهب آخرون إلى أنه على الإباحة . فأما أصحاب الحظر فيلزمون الأضداد التي لا انفكاك عن جميعها، وليس يتحقق العُرُو عن جملتها، فإن حظروا جميعها كان ذلك تكليف ما لا يستطاع، وإن خصصوا بالحظر شيئًا عن شيء من غير تقبيح العقل وتحسينه، لم يخف سقوط هذا المذهب، وإن خصصوا الحظر بما يعتقدون جواز الخلو عنه أصلا،
And al-ilzam: Al-Juwayni defined it as: repelling the opponent's speech by what necessitates a separation between him and what his advocacy included. An example of that is what al-Juwayni objected to every group of the Mu'tazila. He said: The Mu'tazila have split; some of them held that what reason does not specify as bad or good is under prohibition (al-hazr) before revelation, and others held that it is under permissibility (al-ibaha). As for the proponents of prohibition (al-hazr), they necessitate the opposites from which there is no separation from all of them, and freedom from all of them is not realizable. If they prohibit all of them, that would be an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yusta'). If they specify prohibition to some things without reason specifying badness or goodness, the fall of this school is obvious. And if they specify prohibition to what they claim it is possible to be free from originally...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage defines ilzam (necessitation) and provides an example from al-Juwayni against the Mu'tazila. The definition: ilzam is repelling the opponent's speech by what necessitates a separation (fasl) between the opponent and what his advocacy (nusra) included. That is, the dialectician forces the opponent to accept a consequence that contradicts his own position or creates a dilemma. The example concerns the Mu'tazilite dispute over the status of actions before revelation (what al-Shar'). One group held that all actions are prohibited (al-hazr) unless revealed otherwise; another group held they are permitted (al-ibaha). Al-Juwayni attacks the prohibitionists (ashab al-hazr) using ilzam. He says: they (the prohibitionists) 'necessitate the opposites from which there is no separation from all of them'—meaning they are forced to prohibit all possible actions, which leads to an impossible obligation (taklif ma la yusta'), because a person cannot avoid all actions. If they instead specify some actions as prohibited arbitrarily (without rational basis), their school obviously collapses. If they specify prohibition based on what they believe can be avoided entirely, then that also leads to a problem (the text is cut off, but the ilzam is already clear). Al-Juwayni is forcing the Mu'tazila to accept a logical consequence that undermines their doctrine of hazr: either they prohibit everything, which is impossible, or they specify arbitrarily, which is irrational. This is the essence of ilzam: demonstrating that the opponent's position leads to an absurd or impossible conclusion.

Key Terms
الإلزام
الحظر
الإباحة

Key Takeaway
Ilzam is a dialectical technique that forces an opponent to confront a necessary consequence of his position that is absurd or contradictory, thereby weakening his advocacy.

The Method of Qalb (Reversal) in Dialectic
Al-Shirazi uses qalb to refute an opponent's argument about the form of command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qalb method to refute an opponent's argument by turning their own premises against them.

Core Idea
Qalb turns the opponent's own proof against them — using their premises to support your position.

In dialectical debate, the most efficient refutation often comes from turning the opponent's own argument against them. Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi demonstrates this technique, called qalb (reversal), in his refutation of an opponent who claims that the imperative form is linguistically shared (mushtarak) between commanding and prohibiting. By analyzing how al-Shirazi exposes the flaws in the opponent's reasoning, you will learn a powerful tool for Islamic dialectic (jadal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim and evidence
Read the passage and determine what the opponent asserts about the imperative form. The opponent claims the form is shared (mushtarak) between commanding an action and desisting from it. Note the evidence the opponent uses to support this claim.
The opponent's claim: the imperative form is ambiguous, not specific to action.
2
Understand al-Shirazi's reversal strategy
Al-Shirazi does not directly deny the opponent's claim. Instead, he accepts the opponent's framework and asks: how was this shared meaning established? By reason or by transmitted report? He then shows that neither method supports the opponent, thus the argument is reversed.
Al-Shirazi uses the opponent's own methods against him.
3
Analyze the dialectical move
Al-Shirazi argues that if the shared meaning were transmitted, it would have to be mutawatir (widely transmitted) to be credible, but no such transmission exists. If it were based on reason, reason has no say in linguistic meanings. Therefore, the opponent's claim fails, and the same reasoning supports al-Shirazi's position that the imperative is for action.
The reversal works because the opponent's logic applies equally to both sides.
4
Apply qalb to a new example
Think of a debate where an opponent uses an argument that could be turned around. For instance, an opponent says 'Qiyas is invalid because it relies on human opinion.' You can reverse: 'Your argument against qiyas itself relies on a form of reasoning that is not textually established – you are using an analogy (comparing qiyas to something else) to reject qiyas, which is self-defeating.'
The key is to find the common premise that both sides must accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الشيرازي يقول بأن للأمر صيغة موضوعة في اللغة تدل على الفعل، فإنه لم يرتض هذا الاستدلال واعترض عليه بطريق القلب، حيث استخدم هذا الدليل في الاحتجاج على الخصم، وبين أن هذا الدليل هو حجة على الخصم وليس حجة له ، فقال : والجواب : أنا نقلب ذلك عليه في إثبات الاشتراك في هذه الصيغة، فإنه يزعم أنها تحتمل الإقدام وتحتمل الإحجام وهي مشتركة بين الأمرين، فلا يخلو إما أن يكون قد أثبت هذا الاشتراك بالعقل أو بالنقل، فلا يجوز أن يكون بالعقل، لأن العقل لا مجال له في ذلك على ما ذكروا، ولا يجوز أن يكون بالنقل، لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون تواترا لأنه لو وجد لعلمناه ضرورة كما علمنا سائر الأضداد والألفاظ المشتركة كالعين واللون، ولا يجوز أن يكون آحادًا لأن مثل ذلك لا يثبت بأخبار الآحاد ، لأنه يكثر استعماله وتعم البلوى به فلا يكون النقل فيه آحادًا، فكل عذر له في إثبات الاشتراك فهو عذرنا في إثبات كونه صيغة موضوعة لاستدعاء (الفعل)
.1
(1) شرح اللمع، لأبي إسحاق الشيرازي، ج: ص : 203 . (2) الكافية في الجدل، لإمام الحرمين الجويني، ص: 70 .
And because al-Shirazi says that the command has a linguistic form denoting an action, he did not accept this inference and objected to it by the method of qalb (reversal), wherein he used this evidence in arguing against the opponent, and showed that this evidence is a proof against the opponent and not for him. He said: The answer: we reverse that against him in establishing that this form is shared (mushtarak), for he claims that it bears the meaning of undertaking and also the meaning of desisting, and it is shared between the two matters. Then it is inevitable that he either established this shared meaning by reason (aql) or by transmitted report (naql). It is not permissible that it be by reason, because reason has no scope in that according to what they mentioned. And it is not permissible that it be by transmitted report, because it is inevitable that it either be mutawatir, for if it existed we would know it necessarily just as we know other contraries and shared words like 'ayn and lawn, and it cannot be on the authority of individuals (ahad) because such a matter is not established by solitary reports, since its usage is frequent and the need for it is general, so the transmission regarding it cannot be solitary. Therefore every excuse he has for establishing shared meaning is our excuse for establishing that it is a form posited for calling to (action).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage defines the dialectical method of qalb (reversal) as used by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi. The context is a dispute about whether the imperative form in language is specific to commanding an action or shared between commanding and prohibiting (i.e., ambiguous). Al-Shirazi's opponent argues that the imperative form is shared. Al-Shirazi counters by using qalb: he takes the opponent's own argument and turns it against them. The opponent claims the imperative is shared (mushtarak) between action and inaction. Al-Shirazi then asks how this shared meaning is established: by reason or by transmission? Reason cannot decide linguistic meanings, as agreed. Transmission would have to be mutawatir (massive frequency) to be conclusive, but there is no such transmission—if there were, we would know it necessarily, like we know common shared words like عين (eye/spring) and لون (color). It cannot be established by solitary reports because such a widely-used term would require wide transmission. Therefore, the opponent's excuse fails, and the same excuse can be used to argue that the imperative is specifically for calling to action. This exemplifies qalb: using the opponent's reasoning to support one's own position. In Islamic legal theory, qalb is a valid dialectical move, similar to how one might argue that if a certain analogy (qiyas) is accepted for one case, it must apply to another.

Key Terms
القلب
الاشتراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qalb argument, how does al-Shirazi undermine the opponent's claim that the imperative is shared between commanding and prohibiting?
A) By showing that the opponent's proof rests on reason, which is insufficient for language.
B) By demonstrating that the opponent's transmission evidence must be mutawatir, but it is not.
C) By arguing that the imperative can only be for action.
D) By citing a consensus of linguists.

Key Takeaway
Qalb is a powerful dialectical tool that forces the opponent to either accept the reversal or abandon their own premises.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a qalb argument for the following: Your opponent claims that qiyas (analogy) is not a valid source of law because it is based on personal opinion. Using qalb, show that his objection itself relies on an analogy (e.g., comparing qiyas to something else).
?
Practice in a pair: one student takes the position that 'the Quranic text is clear and requires no interpretation,' while the other uses qalb to show that the opponent's assertion itself is an interpretation.

Dialectic -- Jadal
intermediate
5 min
The Correct Application of Ilzam in Dialectic
Al-Juwayni defines ilzam and gives an example against Mu'tazili hazr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid ilzam argument that forces the opponent to a contradiction based on his own premises.

Core Idea
Ilzam forces a contradiction by showing the opponent's own evidence leads away from his claim.

Al-Juwayni defines ilzam as a method to repel the opponent's argument by necessitating a separation between him and his supporting evidence. In this lesson, we examine his first example with the Mu'tazili hazr position to understand how a correct ilzam works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim and evidence
Find the opponent's thesis and the reasons they give. In the example, Mu'tazili hazr claim: actions before revelation are prohibited. Their evidence: reason does not determine good/bad.
2
Show that the evidence leads away from the claim
Al-Juwayni shows that their position leads to impossible obligations or arbitrary distinctions, contradicting their own principle.
3
Verify the ilzam is based on actual premises
Check that the forced contradiction follows from what the opponent actually believes, not a misattribution. Al-Juwayni uses their own reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و - الإلزام :
(1) « عرفه الجويني بأنه : دفع كلام الخصم بما يوجب فصلا بينه وبين ما تضمن نصرته» (2) .
من ذلك ما اعترض به الجويني على كل من فرق المعتزلة ، قال : وقد افترقت المعتزلة، فذهب بعضهم إلى أن ما لا يعين العقل فيه قبحًا ولا حسنًا فهو على الحظر قبل ورود الشرع، وذهب آخرون إلى أنه على الإباحة . فأما أصحاب الحظر فيلزمون الأضداد التي لا انفكاك عن جميعها، وليس يتحقق العُرُو عن جملتها، فإن حظروا جميعها كان ذلك تكليف ما لا يستطاع، وإن خصصوا بالحظر شيئًا عن شيء من غير تقبيح العقل وتحسينه، لم يخف سقوط هذا المذهب، وإن خصصوا الحظر بما يعتقدون جواز الخلو عنه أصلا، (1) فمرجعهم إلى أن التصرف في ملك الغير من غير إذنه قبيح لكن، أحيانا قد يستعمل هذا المسلك الجدلي استعمالا خاطئًا، وذلك حين لا يطلع المجادل على الرأي الحقيقي الكامل لخصمه، فقد يلزمه بما لا يقول به، متوهما أنه يقول به، وذلك كما في صنيع القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني مع المعتزلة القائلين بأن المكره على العبادة لا يجوز أن يكون مكلفا بها، حيث ألزمهم رحمه الله تعالى إثم المكره على القتل، فإنه منهي عنه، آثم به لو أقدم عليه، فقد علق الجويني على صنيع القاضي هذا، بقوله :
وهذه هفوة عظيمة فإنهم لا يمنعون النهي عن الشيء مع الحمل عليه، فإن ذلك أشد في المجنة واقتضاء الثواب وإنما الذي منعوه الاضطرار إلى فعل مع الأمر به » (2).
And - ilzam: (1) Al-Juwayni defined it as: 'Repelling the opponent's speech by what necessitates a separation between him and what his support entails.' (2) An example of that is what al-Juwayni objected to each faction of the Mu'tazila. He said: The Mu'tazila have split: some hold that what reason does not deem bad or good is prohibited before revelation, and others hold that it is permissible. As for the proponents of prohibition, they force contradictory positions that are inseparable from all of them, and freedom from them all is not realized. For if they prohibit all of them, that would be imposing an impossible obligation; if they specify prohibition for some things over others without reason deeming bad or good, the fall of this doctrine is not hidden; and if they specify prohibition for what they believe can be free from it at all, their reference is that disposing of another's property without permission is bad. But sometimes this dialectical method may be used incorrectly, when the disputant does not know the true complete opinion of his opponent, so he may force upon him what he does not hold, imagining that he holds it. That is like the action of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani with the Mu'tazila who said that the person coerced to worship cannot be obligated to perform it, where he forced upon them (may Allah have mercy on him) the sin of the coerced person to kill, for it is prohibited and he would be sinful if he committed it. Al-Juwayni commented on this action of al-Qadi, saying: 'This is a great blunder, for they do not forbid the prohibition of something along with being urged to it, for that is more severe in trial and deserving of reward. What they actually forbid is compulsion to do an act with a command to do it.'
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage explains ilzam (forcing a contradiction or consequence) as a dialectical method. Al-Juwayni defines it as repelling the opponent's argument by showing that it entails a separation between the opponent and his own supporting evidence. In other words, you force the opponent into a position that contradicts his original claim or leads to an absurdity. The first example: The Mu'tazila disagreed on the status of actions before revelation—some said all are prohibited (hazr), others said permissible (ibaha). Al-Juwayni attacks the 'hazr' position by ilzam: they cannot consistently prohibit all actions because that would be impossible (taklif ma la yutaq). If they prohibit some actions arbitrarily, that is baseless. If they prohibit only what can be avoided, they implicitly rely on the principle that using another's property without permission is bad, which is a rational judgment—contradicting their claim that reason does not determine good/bad. So their position collapses. The second example warns against misuse: a disputant may incorrectly attribute a view to the opponent. Al-Baqillani mistakenly forced the Mu'tazila into holding that a coerced killer is sinful, but the Mu'tazila did not say that—they only denied obligation under coercion, not that prohibition and reward cannot coexist. Al-Juwayni corrects this: the Mu'tazila allow prohibition along with urging (as a trial), but not compulsion with a command. This teaches that ilzam must be based on the opponent's true position.

Key Terms
الإلزام (al-ilzam): A dialectical method defined by al-Juwayni as repelling the opponent's argument by showing it entails a separation from his supportive evidence; forcing a contradiction or absurdity. [Note: In later adab al-bahth works, ilzam is often a sub-type of mu'arada. Al-Juwayni's definition here is specific to jadal.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, what is the correct use of ilzam in dialectic?
A) To attribute any contradiction to the opponent regardless of his actual statements.
B) To show that the opponent's own evidence leads to a separation from his claim.
C) To force the opponent to accept your own proof.
D) To cite a consensus against the opponent.

Key Takeaway
A valid ilzam forces a contradiction based on the opponent's own premises, not a misrepresentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct an ilzam against the Mu'tazili ibaha position (all actions before revelation are permissible) using al-Juwayni's method. What contradiction would you force? Hint: ibaha would allow harmful actions, which even Mu'tazila would reject.
